  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_81a2fc13-9f2b-41a3-87a6-05d5c1db6532'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText15575567724294183678" style="display:none"><i>“I made the wrong choice.”</i><br /><br />Lina is spending the summer in Tuscany, but she isn’t in the mood for Italy’s famous sunshine and fairy-tale landscape. She’s only there because it was her mother’s dying wish that she get to know her father. But what kind of father isn’t around for sixteen years? All Lina wants to do is go back home.<br /><br />But then she is given a journal that her mom had kept when she lived in Italy. Suddenly Lina’s uncovering a magical world of secret romances, art, and hidden bakeries. A world that inspires her, along with the ever-so-charming Ren, to follow in her mother’s footsteps and unearth a secret that has been kept for far too long. It’s a secret that will change everything she knew about her mother, her father—and even herself.<br /><br />People come to Italy for love and gelato, someone tells her, but sometimes they discover much more.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, it absolutely is. Jenna Evans Welch comes from a strong Christian background, so there's lots of wholesomeness here, but she doesn't bring religi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, it absolutely is. Jenna Evans Welch comes from a strong Christian background, so there's lots of wholesomeness here, but she doesn't bring religion into the story. There is no moral preachiness to be found. It is just simply clean, wistful fun. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2100983943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2100983943" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2100983943?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481432559" href="/book/show/32333322-love-gelato">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100983943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5761711238876689456"><b>
  <i>‘people come to italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, its for the same two things - love and getalo.’</i>
</b><br/><br/><u>some personal news:</u> im moving to italy at the end of the week and i would be lying if i said this book didnt influence that decision. <br/><br/>im off to find my own ren to love, eat my entire body weight in gelato, and live my best dolce vita. <3<br/><br/>________________________________________<br/><br/>sugar and spice and everything nice - that is what this book is made of. and now i have a toothache from</span>
  <span id="freeText5761711238876689456" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘people come to italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, its for the same two things - love and getalo.’</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>some personal news:</u> im moving to italy at the end of the week and i would be lying if i said this book didnt influence that decision. <br /><br />im off to find my own ren to love, eat my entire body weight in gelato, and live my best dolce vita. &lt;3<br /><br />________________________________________<br /><br />sugar and spice and everything nice - that is what this book is made of. and now i have a toothache from the sticky sweetness of this story, which is <u>exactly</u> what you would expect from a title like <i>‘love and gelato.’</i><br /><br />this book checks so many boxes for me, i dont even know where to begin. so let me share my list:<br /><br /> - coming of age story (love the connection between lina and her mothers journal). <b>check.</b><br /> - set abroad (ughh. how romantic is italy!? <i>sigh</i>). <b>check.</b><br /> - swoon-worthy crush (pls marry me, ren, i luv u). <b>check.</b><br /> - fun adventures, amazing characters, and heartfelt message. <b>check, check, check!</b><br /><br />im in awe at how something so light and fluffy can deliver such a deep and meaningful story. everything about this is positively wonderful and absolutely lovely. this gave me heart flutters and butterflies and all the warm fuzzy feels imaginable. its definitely going to the top of my favourite contemporaries of all time - its the ultimate feel book book! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1717881435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1717881435" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1717881435?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=summer-reads">summer-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1717881435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15778852724647608825"><i>
  <blockquote>‘‘You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it’s for the same two things.’’<br/>‘‘What?’’<br/>‘‘Love and gelato.’’</blockquote>
</i><strong> </strong><br/><strong>WARNING: </strong><em>Love & Gelato </em>may trigger a dizzying yearning for gelato. I repeat, <em>Love & Gelato </em>may trigger a dizzying yearning for gelato. <strong>Beware, readers! </strong><br/><br/><strong>3.5 stars. </strong>It may also make you crave to find love in Italy…<br/><br/>This contemporary novel is exactly what I needed after finishing a frightening thriller novel – <em>Behind Closed Doors</em>. It took my mind off negativ</span>
  <span id="freeText15778852724647608825" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>‘‘You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it’s for the same two things.’’<br />‘‘What?’’<br />‘‘Love and gelato.’’</blockquote>
</i><strong> </strong><br /><strong>WARNING: </strong><em>Love &amp; Gelato </em>may trigger a dizzying yearning for gelato. I repeat, <em>Love &amp; Gelato </em>may trigger a dizzying yearning for gelato. <strong>Beware, readers! </strong><br /><br /><strong>3.5 stars. </strong>It may also make you crave to find love in Italy…<br /><br />This contemporary novel is exactly what I needed after finishing a frightening thriller novel – <em>Behind Closed Doors</em>. It took my mind off negative thoughts about life and marriage.<br /><br />It’s a<strong> romantic and mysterious</strong> story starring a very lively American girl who is sent to her father’s house in Italy by her grandmother after her mother succumbed to cancer.<br /><br /><strong> The theme of family is ever present.</strong> When Lina arrives in Italy, she is given her mother’s journal for when she studied photography there.<br /><br />Lina not only wants to understand what happened between her mother and Howard – why they are not together anymore – but she also wants to feel closer to her mother by doing so.<br /><br /><strong>It’s very heartfelt.</strong> I especially enjoyed the snippets of her mother’s life in Italy. While her story is indeed saddening, there is good that comes out of it.<br /><br />Lina also meets a charming male fellow living next d—field to her. Ren is sweet and respectful and open and generous – I took a like to him. While there is a <strong>mild love-triangle situation going on</strong>, it’s easy to discard it from one’s mind.<br /><br />So that’s the good part. The no-so-great part is the <strong>cluelessness and confusion</strong>. If there’s one thing I’m annoyed with is when a character refuses or can’t see the obvious in front of her and has to go through great lengths or experience painful events to discover what was always crystal obvious.<br /><br />In other words, <strong>I dislike clueless characters</strong>, and Lina is definitely one of them. Furthermore, the whole ‘‘who is my father?’’ situation didn’t need to be that complicated. And it’s not that it’s <em>complicated </em>per se, but the author made it so. She deliberately confuses us!<br /><br /><u>To some extent</u>, I love being played with and being able to guess things for myself, but when someone is actually making me walk circles over and over again—no, thank you.<br /><br />I had fun with <em>Love &amp; Gelato. </em>The setting is gorgeous, the main characters are heart-warming and the adventures pretty darn diverting. <strong>It’s not impressive, but it sure is a pleasant summer read</strong>.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15778852724647608825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196783440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13532933420474369111"><b><br/>RIP Me.</b> <br/><br/>I have officially drowned in sugar.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509478782ra/24325820.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This <b>
  <u>super cute</u>
</b> YA Contemporary was everything I was looking for and more.<br/> <br/><b>Funny, witty, romantic and delicious</b>, I loved every moment of experiencing Italy with Lena. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493989517ra/22673866.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The found family elements were extremely well done and I appreciated the love and friendships so much. <br/><br/>My only disappointment is that I waited so long to read it. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546961482ra/26885210.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></span>

<div id="review_2476449764" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2476449764" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2476449764?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=contemporary-read">contemporary-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2476449764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15815884183292559498"><b>
  <i>“You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it’s for the same two things.”<br/>“What?”<br/>“Love and gelato.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>The story narrated in this book is one of friendship, family, and first love. The characters enhanced the concept at the core of this book and the dynamic between each of them was written very well. <br/><br/>Lina, after facing the trauma of losing her mother, flies to Italy for the summer in order to fulfill her mother’s last wish. Her mother also seemed to arrange for </span>
  <span id="freeText15815884183292559498" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it’s for the same two things.”<br />“What?”<br />“Love and gelato.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The story narrated in this book is one of friendship, family, and first love. The characters enhanced the concept at the core of this book and the dynamic between each of them was written very well. <br /><br />Lina, after facing the trauma of losing her mother, flies to Italy for the summer in order to fulfill her mother’s last wish. Her mother also seemed to arrange for her to live with Howard, her mother’s friend from her days in college. After her mother passes, her grandmother informs her that her mother left out the minute detail that Howard also happens to be her father.<br />Now in Italy, she finds out that Howard, who refuses to refer to as her dad, lives in a graveyard. Not the ideal place for a girl who just lost her mother. Struggling with her mother’s death and trying to accept that Howard is her father, she tries to cope with her situation for the summer.<br /><br />As the story progresses, the author takes us through Italy in the protagonist’s attempt to understand her mother’s year in college. After Lina’s arrival in Florence, she is handed her mother’s old journal, one she has never seen before, which she has never seen before, which is weird because her mother is extremely open about her journals and is well known for her entertaining writing. In an attempt to see Florence through her mother’s eyes, she makes her way through the town with the guidance of the journal. And she has come to realise that her mother’s college years were unlike anything she imagined.<br /><br />A romance the seemed to have ended badly, a proclamation that could change everything, and the story of a vibrant woman making her way through life, her mother may have secrets of her own. The journal allows her to finally understand the piece of her mother’s life she has never known about, and maybe even why she never knew her father.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Maybe that was just part of the Italian experience. Come to Italy. Fall in love. Watch everything blow up in your face.</i>
</b><br /><br />Since her mother’s journal is inserted into the book, we follow not one but to women making their way through Florence and finding love. Watching her cope with her mother’s death and come to peace with her life as it is now is amazing. We watch her open herself to the possibility of a life in Florence and makes a friend through a very unusual set of circumstances.<br /><br />Now that I have finished reading this book, the title seems to the most endearing thing about it because a story with such depth can only be described by Love and Gelato, and anything else wouldn’t seem right. The characters were amazing, the description of the city was perfect, the relationship between the characters and the city was written lovingly and overall there is nothing I would change about this book.<br /><br />I’m undeniably, inexplicably, explicitly in love with this book and I wish everyone who likes contemporary books would read this precious gem of a story because reading this book is, right now, one of the best experiences of my life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15815884183292559498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer480800726471422503"><b> FOR THE LOVE OF ALL THAT'S HOLY!! </b><br/><br/>I'm usually not this hysterical but my heart has been shattered, my eyes are warm with tears and I don't even have half the idea of what I'm typing because I can't see properly (I even shelved it as "Indian mythology" so you probably get the idea) but this is totally me trying to weave words into a coherent sentence. I don't think I will be able to do justice to this book but I have to let out everything before my nerves get the better of me. So here goes nothi</span>
  <span id="freeText480800726471422503" style="display:none"><b> FOR THE LOVE OF ALL THAT'S HOLY!! </b><br /><br />I'm usually not this hysterical but my heart has been shattered, my eyes are warm with tears and I don't even have half the idea of what I'm typing because I can't see properly (I even shelved it as "Indian mythology" so you probably get the idea) but this is totally me trying to weave words into a coherent sentence. I don't think I will be able to do justice to this book but I have to let out everything before my nerves get the better of me. So here goes nothing. <br /><br />Seventeen y/o Lina loses her mom to pancreatic cancer. But she has to fulfill her mom's dying wish that she spend a summer(and maybe longer) in Tuscany. Lina travels halfway around the world to stay with her father Howard, who is the caretaker of a cemetery just outside Florence. But as she is given an old journal of her mother's, she gets to know things about her mother she had no clue about before and must deal with the grief and heartbreak threatening to consume her. As Lina has her own romantic life to endure, with her mother's journal as a cautionary tale, she is faced with a decision to make, and it could very well be a life-changing one. <br /><br />To say that this book found its way to the very core of my heart would be a huge betrayal to Six Of Crows, Simon vs The Homosapiens agenda, Eliza and her Monsters and ACOTAR trilogy (my all-time favourites). But it definitely does make me question every other book I've rated five stars, because it's certainly not fair to this book. <br /><br />This book is wonderfully enamoured with hope, love and every other cute, light-hearted feeling one can come up with. But most importantly, it is a tale about strength and healing, about <b>enduring</b> despite everything that life throws your way. To realise that there is dusk, but also dawn. That no matter how many heartbreaks or failures you endure, no matter how many of those moments-that-will-blow-your-composure exist or how many times you're thrown off balance, they'll soon evaporate and things will move in a better direction. All that's needed is to hold on and never let go, because enduring isn't something that's in-built, it's something you do. <br /> <b> <i> "Every new beginning comes from some other beginning's end" </i></b> <br /><br />This book to me is exactly how <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14115788.Jenna_Evans_Welch" title="Jenna Evans Welch" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenna Evans Welch</a>describes Florence. <br /> <b> <i> "Florence is exactly how I thought it would be and nothing like it at all. It is absolutely magical and yet it's gritty too. I've never been anyplace I want to capture so much." </i></b> <br /><br /> I want to visit Italy more than ever with Ren and Howard as my tourist guides for the same two reasons:<br /><br /><b>Love and Gelato </b></span>

  <span id="freeText6269878911772572647" style="display:none">3.5 ⭐️<br /><br />This was cute. It was 100% what I expected, but ever so slightly better. Carolina AKA Lina has been sent to live in Florence with her father after the death of her mother, a father she has never met or even heard of, until now. <div id="review_2761627746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2761627746" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2761627746?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2761627746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer859737973612759880">"You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it's for the same two things...love and gelato."<br/><br/>Lina is only in Italy because of a promise she made to her mother on her deathbed.<br/><br/>She isn't moved by the country's beauty—she's having too difficult a time dealing with the fact that she's going to be living WITH HER FATHER (about whom she never knew anything), much less living in a house in the midst of a famous cemetery, because he is the caretaker.<br/><br/>Why didn't her mother</span>
  <span id="freeText859737973612759880" style="display:none">"You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it's for the same two things...love and gelato."<br /><br />Lina is only in Italy because of a promise she made to her mother on her deathbed.<br /><br />She isn't moved by the country's beauty—she's having too difficult a time dealing with the fact that she's going to be living WITH HER FATHER (about whom she never knew anything), much less living in a house in the midst of a famous cemetery, because he is the caretaker.<br /><br />Why didn't her mother ever tell her anything about her father? What could have happened 16 years ago that would have been so bad that she not only fled Italy, but she never returned, and never made contact with the man again? All Lina wants is answers, and what she knows she doesn't want is to spend time getting to know Howard, umm, her father, or settle in—she's ready to head back to the U.S. and move back in with her best friend, Addie.<br /><br />But little by little, Italy's charm starts to wear her down, and so does Ren, the handsome Italian-American boy who lives not too far away. And when Lina gets her hands on her mother's journal from the time she spent in Italy, she's determined to find everything she can about why her mother kept so much a secret from her, and why she left this magical place and a man she was supposedly in love with.<br /><br />"Maybe that was just part of the Italian experience. Come to Italy. Fall in love. Watch everything blow up in your face. You could probably read about it on travel websites."<br /><br />The deeper she gets into her mother's journal, the more confusing things become. It looks like her mother was an expert at keeping secrets, and if they're revealed, they could be painful for some. So with Ren as her sidekick, she embarks on a journey to trace her mother's steps and figure out the path her love story took—no matter what the consequences. And along the way she understands just how her mother fell in love with such a beautiful country, and how complicated the line between love and friendship can become.<br /><br />Having just read a fairly emotional book, I was looking for something lighter and fun. <b>
  <i>Love &amp; Gelato</i>
</b> totally hit the spot—it was sweet, well-written, and I fell totally in love with it. It was a YA novel that certainly didn't feel like one, and yet the characters spoke like teenagers, not like sarcastic comedians.<br /><br />Jenna Evans Welch's prose made this novel sparkle like the Italian countryside, and her imagery was tremendously evocative. There really isn't anything surprising in this novel—not even the "surprise" that Lina discovers—but that doesn't matter. <b>
  <i>Love &amp; Gelato</i>
</b> has so much charm, heart, and romance at its core that I flew through the book, and now I'm sad that it's all over.<br /><br />If you're feeling like you need a change of pace from brooding thrillers or family dysfunction, <b>
  <i>Love &amp; Gelato</i>
</b> may be just what <i>il medico</i> ordered! I know I'll be reading Welch's new book when it's released in May.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="859737973612759880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1710501376" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1710501376" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1710501376?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=best-covers">best-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=d-n-f">d-n-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=literal-trash">literal-trash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=annoying-female-leads">annoying-female-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=savage-review">savage-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710501376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14405213529360228121"><b>DNF @ 10%</b><br/><br/><i>I will be displaying my emotions through Ron Swanson gifs.</i><br/><br/><i>Love and Gelato</i> was a book I desperately wanted to love. I mean, the set up was perfect. Italy, love and gelato (which I've never actually had but it sounds good). Italy is a destination I have always wanted to travel, and how could you not with all the culture present in the cities. <br/><br/>However, as I began to read this book I knew it wasn't going to be a finish for me. Why? Well, the writing just jumped straight into the plot withou</span>
  <span id="freeText14405213529360228121" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 10%</b><br><br><i>I will be displaying my emotions through Ron Swanson gifs.</i><br><br><i>Love and Gelato</i> was a book I desperately wanted to love. I mean, the set up was perfect. Italy, love and gelato (which I've never actually had but it sounds good). Italy is a destination I have always wanted to travel, and how could you not with all the culture present in the cities. <br><br>However, as I began to read this book I knew it wasn't going to be a finish for me. Why? Well, the writing just jumped straight into the plot without any other pretenses or introductions, straight to the fact a house was in a cemetery. Then, we have one of the protagonists, <b>Lina</b>, first line:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It's a cemetery." My voice was like weak tea. </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473320503ra/20445900.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>What? What in the name of all things holy and blessed does this mean? Is weak tea really the metaphor you choose to use? I knew this book, and I would have a problem here almost instantly. I can handle crazy metaphors sometimes, but this was a no and was at the very beginning of the book, so it could only go downhill. For me, it did. <br><br>Not only did my hatred for Lina become cemented in the first 100 pages of the 900 page eBook <b>but</b> I was subjected to countless more strange and "quirky" people. However, Lina was just <b>rude</b>. I understand her mum had died six months previously, and it seemed like that was leading up to be an excuse featuring through the rest of the book, but she was rude. She was unwilling to give her recently discovered father a chance. I don't understand why because she isn't even sure if he knew about her existence. <br><br>Also:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Aggressively normal."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452881231ra/17756120.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Is a sentence I never want to hear again because <i>what?</i><br><br>Oh, we also get to introduced to Lina's totally <s>tacky</s> awesome best friend, who is like <i>so</i> <s>idiotic</s> funny. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Why are you being so quiet? Is Gravedigger there?”<br>“I’m in my bedroom, but I get the feeling that sound travels in this house. I don’t know if he can hear me or not.”<br>“Great. So you can’t even speak freely. We’d better come up with a code word so I know if you’re okay. Say ‘bluebird’ if you’re being held hostage.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473321110ra/20446015.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Like Ron's burger, this <b>completely</b> missed the mark for me. <br><br>Oh, and lets not forget that Addie and Lina are both very <s>judgmental</s> creative:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Addie and I had once won a costume contest dressed as Tacky Tourists. These two could have been our inspiration.”</i>
</blockquote> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473321110i/20446016.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I can't even add onto that. I understand there is a "tacky tourist" look, but honestly, if I went travelling I would probably be a tacky tourist myself and guess what? <i>That is fine.</i><br><br>Now, one last quote before I conclude this review. The quote that made me decide this was not for me in any way:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Howard still had steam curling out of his nostrils.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473321110ra/20446017.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I understand some people may think I didn't give this book a fair go, considering I decided to DNF at 10%, but honestly, I couldn't subject myself to this. I couldn't put myself through head banging sentences and characters who are meant to be funny and different but are simply rude. It's possible this story is <u>super</u> cute, but I won't be sticking around to find out. <br><br>Honestly, what this book felt like was a jumble of words that shouldn't have slipped past an editor, in my opinion. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473321110i/20446018.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14405213529360228121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2036047305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=charming-af-male-lead">charming-af-male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=young-love">young-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53967892-the-girl-murdered-by-her-tbr?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036047305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318851627281273375">5-I-NEED-AN-ITALIAN-DUDE-RIGHT-NOW-STARS!!!<br/><br/>This book was successful in getting rid of my sucky reading slump. After a month of force reading various books, this book performed its magic and voila! Reading slump gone. I never thought that a super cute young-adult contemporary romance is what I really need. This was the first contemporary book I've read this year and I absolutely adored it. The plot, characters, and setting were captivating.<br/><br/>The setting of the story is in Italy. Oh gosh, Italy... I</span>
  <span id="freeText5318851627281273375" style="display:none">5-I-NEED-AN-ITALIAN-DUDE-RIGHT-NOW-STARS!!!<br /><br />This book was successful in getting rid of my sucky reading slump. After a month of force reading various books, this book performed its magic and voila! Reading slump gone. I never thought that a super cute young-adult contemporary romance is what I really need. This was the first contemporary book I've read this year and I absolutely adored it. The plot, characters, and setting were captivating.<br /><br />The setting of the story is in Italy. Oh gosh, Italy... I really really want to go to Italy. I loved that the author wrote a vivid description about Italy. I learned a lot of Italian things thanks to this book. The food, the culture, the history, the people, and the places. I love it all.<br /><br />The plot was simple yet gripping. It wasn't super complicated, which I figured was the best one for a person who's slumping. The pace of the story was set in a normal pace. It tackled about the importance of love, family, regrets, and hope. <br /><br />I also loved the characters. I had some issues with Lina on the first part of the book, she was a little bit bratty and selfish but that was understandable because her whole life was turned upside down because of the big reveal from her mother and grandmother. I actually liked how persevering, brave and adventurous she is. Ren is so charming. He is an Italian-American boy who lives nearby. He helped Lina with revealing the truth about her mother's past life in Italy. I really loved the personality of Ren, he's just the chill, cheerful, and adorable guy who decided to show Lina how beautiful Italy is.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. The writing style was very catchy and uncomplicated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5318851627281273375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1895978370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1895978370" />
    <a title="Sab" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7739510-sab"><img alt="Sab" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589923037p2/7739510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1895978370?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sab" href="/user/show/7739510-sab">Sab</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7739510-sab?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1895978370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2675091821387743703">This is not something I usually do. I don't write reviews. But I really have to get something out of my chest: I am SO TIRED of American authors writing books about Italy/Italian people without even bothering to double-check what the hell they are talking about.<br/>So the main character is Lina (really? Is it supposed to be a popular Italian name?). Her mother dies of cancer and she has to move to Italy to live with her estranged father. So she arrives to her father's house (that is in the middle of</span>
  <span id="freeText2675091821387743703" style="display:none">This is not something I usually do. I don't write reviews. But I really have to get something out of my chest: I am SO TIRED of American authors writing books about Italy/Italian people without even bothering to double-check what the hell they are talking about.<br />So the main character is Lina (really? Is it supposed to be a popular Italian name?). Her mother dies of cancer and she has to move to Italy to live with her estranged father. So she arrives to her father's house (that is in the middle of cemetery ?? okay) and that's when it starts getting reaaaally annoying.<br />She meets Sonia, her dad's assistant (or something like that), and OF COURSE Sonia is a "tall, gazelle-like woman with coffee-colored skin and rows of gold bracelets on each arm. Gorgeous." OF COURSE. I mean. Italians are all tall, beautiful gazelle-like people with coffee-colored skin. Even those who live in Tuscany (which is center-northern Italy, fyi). That's why I'm as pale as a ghost.<br />Anyway. They sit to have dinner (the table OF COURSE was “set with a red-checkered cloth”), lasagna and garlic bread (come on guys, garlic bread is so an American thing) and her father informs her that she can't FaceTime her best friend because "Italy isn’t exactly on the cutting edge of technology” (I mean REALLY? You do realize that it's 2017 in Italy as well?). And then he offers her wine because "Italy doesn’t have a drinking age" which is SO untrue I MEAN WHAT HELL? Get your facts straight. <br />That's when I decided to DNF the book. At, like, page 25. If I could give "Love &amp; Gelato" 0 stars I honestly would.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2675091821387743703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14451126-the-candid-cover-olivia-lori?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1388233196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17172598630238423549"><a title='Full Review on The Candid Cover' href='https://candidcover.net/love-gelato-jenna-evans-welch/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Full Review on The Candid Cover</a><br/><br/>4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Love and Gelato is the perfect book to enjoy this summer. Set in Italy, this book is absolutely breathtaking. The fact that there are old journal entries in the story makes it so much more incredible. Trust me, after reading this book, you’ll be craving some gelato!<br/><br/>Love and Gelato has such an interesting concept! This book tells the story of Lina, a girl who moves to Italy after her mom dies. When she gets there, she is given an old journal of her mom’s an</span>
  <span id="freeText17172598630238423549" style="display:none"><a title="Full Review on The Candid Cover" href="https://candidcover.net/love-gelato-jenna-evans-welch/" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Review on The Candid Cover</a><br /><br />4.5 Stars<br /><br />Love and Gelato is the perfect book to enjoy this summer. Set in Italy, this book is absolutely breathtaking. The fact that there are old journal entries in the story makes it so much more incredible. Trust me, after reading this book, you’ll be craving some gelato!<br /><br />Love and Gelato has such an interesting concept! This book tells the story of Lina, a girl who moves to Italy after her mom dies. When she gets there, she is given an old journal of her mom’s and learns many secrets about her. I really enjoyed reading about Lina’s journey across Italy as she tries to solve the mystery of the journal. She gets herself into many sticky situations, but also makes some really amazing friends along the way. This book was the perfect thing to kick back with in the warm weather.<br /><br />I absolutely adored the Italian setting in Love and Gelato. The way the shops and the landmarks are described is absolutely breathtaking, and I wish I could experience it all in real life! The Italian culture in the book really intrigued me, and I actually learned a few phrases while reading. I have wanted to visit Italy my whole life, and reading this book made me want to go even more!<br /><br />The journaling aspects in Love and Gelato really drew me in. I love the idea of finding an old journal, and discovering that this book incorporated that got me really excited. I enjoyed how the journal entries were added gradually into the book—slowly, then all at once. As Lina warms up to the idea of learning more about her mom, she eventually reads more and more of it. Something about that made me love the story even more.<br /><br />Love and Gelato tells the story of a girl who is given her mom’s old journal and is set in Italy. The journal entries that were slowly added into the book were very enjoyable to read! I would definitely recommend this book, as it is perfect for the summer season.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer105094216594794788">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/>Or mediocre book pics at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.instagram.com/kellyandthebookboar/'>https://www.instagram.com/kellyandthe...</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it's for the same two things."<br/><br/>"What?"<br/><br/>"Love and gelato."</i>
</b><br/><br/>When 16-year old Lina’s mother passes away from pancreatic cancer, she is encouraged by her grandmother to spend the summer in Tuscany in order to get to know Howard – a father she never even knew existed. Lina would have never guessed </span>
  <span id="freeText105094216594794788" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br>Or mediocre book pics at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/kellyandthebookboar/">https://www.instagram.com/kellyandthe...</a><br><br><b>
  <i>"You know, people come to Italy for all sorts of reasons, but when they stay, it's for the same two things."<br><br>"What?"<br><br>"Love and gelato."</i>
</b><br><br>When 16-year old Lina’s mother passes away from pancreatic cancer, she is encouraged by her grandmother to spend the summer in Tuscany in order to get to know Howard – a father she never even knew existed. Lina would have never guessed she’d end up living in a cemetery, or that her mother left a journal regarding her own time spent in Italy or that she would be uncovering a huge secret during her summer abroad.<br><br><i>Love and Gelato</i> was an instant “yes please” due to the title and adorable cover. The story was a little bit . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528725645ra/25720317.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And a little bit of this . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528725645ra/25720318.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<span id="freeTextContainer631173034932409882">This was a cute story about a girl finding a way to move on with life after losing her mother. Lina made a promise to her dying mother, finding herself in Italy with a father she had never met. Lina’s experience tugged at all the right strings for me.<br/><br/>What brought my overall enjoyment down, though, was the diary her mother left for her. Actually, that’s not true. The diary itself didn’t bother me, especially once the story came full circle. No, what drove me bananas was the way Lina chose to read</span>
  <span id="freeText631173034932409882" style="display:none">This was a cute story about a girl finding a way to move on with life after losing her mother. Lina made a promise to her dying mother, finding herself in Italy with a father she had never met. Lina’s experience tugged at all the right strings for me.<br /><br />What brought my overall enjoyment down, though, was the diary her mother left for her. Actually, that’s not true. The diary itself didn’t bother me, especially once the story came full circle. No, what drove me bananas was the way Lina chose to read it a bit at a time in dribs and drabs. I’m sorry... but if I was thrust into the arms of an unknown father in a country I had never been to, you can bet I would be reading that diary cover to cover to get some answers. I just didn’t buy that Lina was too overcome with grief to keep reading.<br /><br />So while I enjoyed reading about Lina’s experiences in Italy, having her mother’s diary interspersed with the story irritated me and had me wanting to skim at parts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="631173034932409882" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1564393003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6033276140397998180">Love & Gelato was a cute, quick, summer read and just what I needed for the plane journey, on which I read it from start to finish but unfortunately, despite this, I didn't fall in love with it.<br/><br/>I didn't really warm to<br/>the characters or feel any strong connection towards them(other than Howard who was a sweetheart) and overall I just couldn't get past the incredibly short time period this book was set over, considering the amount of events that occurred. I've never been a fan of instalove and espe</span>
  <span id="freeText6033276140397998180" style="display:none">Love &amp; Gelato was a cute, quick, summer read and just what I needed for the plane journey, on which I read it from start to finish but unfortunately, despite this, I didn't fall in love with it.<br /><br />I didn't really warm to<br />the characters or feel any strong connection towards them(other than Howard who was a sweetheart) and overall I just couldn't get past the incredibly short time period this book was set over, considering the amount of events that occurred. I've never been a fan of instalove and especially not when that 'instalove' becomes 'actual' love after less than a week?! I mean sure, maybe this guy was super cute but going to a strangers house to meet their mother within a few minutes of first meeting?! STRANGER DANGER PEOPLE!! (I've suddenly become super aware of how old I feel right now... 😅) That being said, if you're a fan of instalove, I'm sure you'd very much enjoy this book! I also found that the characters read very young and Lina's excessive use of the word 'like' felt like a bit of an overkill in trying to make her sound even younger. There were also a few ableist phrases used that I wasn't a fan of at all.<br /><br />Having said all this, I didn't dislike this book. I thought the journal entries and family storyline was an interesting element. I adored the Italian setting and the in depth descriptions of Tuscany, Florence etc. I also very much appreciated the delicious goody descriptions. I don't think I've ever craved Nutella so much in my life. It was fun, it was cute and incredibly easy read and one I'm sure would be the perfect summer read for younger teens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6033276140397998180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="K. Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17568354-k-elizabeth"><img alt="K. Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606078931p2/17568354.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=cute-and-or-easy-reads">cute-and-or-easy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17568354-k-elizabeth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2064680318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11240583609583000366">★<b> 3.75 / 5 </b>★<br/><br/>Ya’ll. This book got me out of my reading slump. I’m <i>super</i> thankful for those of you who recommended it!<br/><br/>Also, I think it’s official: I like Romance novels. Well. Not straight-up Romance, but books like <i>Love and Gelato</i> where it’s contemporary mixed-in with humor, reliable characters, and an adorable romance — count me in (and recommend me more books, haha). I’m not ashamed to say that! These books are addictive.<br/><br/>As someone who travels to Europe for 2-3 months every year, I enjoyed Jenn</span>
  <span id="freeText11240583609583000366" style="display:none">★<b> 3.75 / 5 </b>★<br /><br />Ya’ll. This book got me out of my reading slump. I’m <i>super</i> thankful for those of you who recommended it!<br /><br />Also, I think it’s official: I like Romance novels. Well. Not straight-up Romance, but books like <i>Love and Gelato</i> where it’s contemporary mixed-in with humor, reliable characters, and an adorable romance — count me in (and recommend me more books, haha). I’m not ashamed to say that! These books are addictive.<br /><br />As someone who travels to Europe for 2-3 months every year, I enjoyed Jenna Welch’s accurate depiction of Italy. Their gelato really <i>is</i> that good; and yes, everyone really does walk everywhere. So the little things Lena noticed as an “American tourist” were entirely realistic. <br /><br />Ah. It all sounds good, right? Well, not everything was. A few things that brought down the rating were how predictable the events were, for one. The whole Thomas crushing on Lena and making Ren jealous and “issues” with her actual father… I called all of it. Doesn’t mean it wasn’t enjoyable to read though. <br /><br />The writing, in turn, was good and simple. Almost <i>too</i> simple, since it left little to imagine. But, hey, I’m not complaining.<br /><br /><b>Overall,</b> this was yet another book going into my “cute and easy” reads. I’m going to have to get the second book sometime soon. I heard it’s just as enjoyable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11240583609583000366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3773219863756261668">*4.5 stars*<br/><br/>After finishing this book, (well also during reading it) I had major cravings for some gelato. It was super cute and mysterious. I couldn't put it down! Because of this book, I want to go to Italy even more now.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SdD5Eyp/2sW6Hi5No0/Qa/PdxNwsiYMVNc93ZHw3PZAWVJvj5mSgWf0kjb02w9FztZePMlz78vMnEpOMmGjkqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tZj5STRhzgE1uBW/gk8FgU6Vgn/LhrYCwbWy3o6aSCnqHJu5+Hq0nXKCtk8XwwSZCN/Jkbv0x+TTaFY2asWREw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer17804476770929600104">Jenna Evans Welch was the kind of insatiable child reader who had no choice but to grow up to become a writer. She is the New York Times Bestselling author of LOVE & GELATO and the upcoming LOVE & LUCK. When she isn’t writing girl abroad stories, Jenna can be found chasing her children or making elaborate messes in the kitchen. She lives in Salt Lake City, Utah with her husband and two young child</span>

When she isn’t writing girl abroad stories, Jenna can be found chasing her children or making elaborate messes in the kitchen. She lives in Salt Lake City, Utah with her husband and two young children. </span>
